GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 50.01 INTENT AND PURPOSE.
   It is the intent of the town to provide for the town residents a
comprehensive refuse collection service consisting of regular pickups of
containerized garbage and household rubbish from the curb or street line at
each residence, commercial, or other property.
(Ord. 1977-16, passed 11-7-77)
§ 50.02 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   BIDDER. The person or corporation submitting a bid proposal for service
outlined herein.
   CONTRACTOR. The person or corporation with whom the town enters into a
contract for services outlined herein.
   CURB LINE. Edge of street or alley, if no curb exists.
   DWELLING UNIT. A single-family residence and each apartment shall be
considered a separate family residence; also, each trailer is to be a single-
family residence.
   GARBAGE. All refuse of animal, fish, fowl, fruit, or vegetable matter that
results from the  preparation, use, cooking, retail, or wholesale dealing in,
or storing of meat, fish, fowl, fruit, or vegetable and shall exclude offals,
trimmings, and scraps of butcher shops or meat markets. It shall further mean
and include tin cans, glass, bottles, and broken crockery which have been used
as food or beverage holders.
   HOUSEHOLD RUBBISH. Household goods, refuse, furniture, springs, mattresses,
tin cans, bottles, crockery, broken glass, rags, grass cuttings, and other
similar debris, hedge cuttings, and shrubbery trimmings bundled, boxed, or
otherwise contained, furnace pipe, stoves, water boilers, trunks, incinerator
refuse and cold ashes of all kinds, wood not over 36 inches in length, all
rubbish, trash, debris, waste, litter, scrap, packings, excelsior, straw, metal
cooking utensils, toys, porcelain, carpeting, leather, rubber, shoes, clothing,
cardboard, household appliances, tree trimmings, trees, and broken limbs under
36 inches in length. Excluded will be garbage, broken concrete, and other
refuse from repairs, alterations, and new construction of buildings and
sidewalks, tree limbs, and trunks over 30 inches in length, debris from
commercial or industrial establishments, and material which cannot be handled
easily by two men.
    OPEN GATE DUMPING PRIVILEGE. Any resident of the town shall have free
access to contractor’s landfill at all times without extra charge, excluding
commercial trash haulers.
   RESIDENCE or PROPERTY. Business and/or commercial property.
   RUBBISH. All rags, broken glass, crockery bottles, tin cans, paper, grass
cuttings and similar household refuse, including cold ashes from incinerators,
burners, heating plants and stoves. Generally included are household discards
that can be contained in a covered 30 gallon container or plastic bags.
(Ord. 1977-16, passed 11-7-77)
§ 50.03 INSPECTIONS.
   The Town Council shall designate a town employee as inspector to investigate
complaints of missed garbage or rubbish pick-ups. The contractor shall check
with the town office weekly. If the missed units are not picked up the
following day after being reported and confirmed by the inspector, the
inspector shall be authorized, upon good cause, to levy a fine or penalty of $5
against the contractor per pick-up or unit missed, the same to be paid or
credited at the next succeeding pay date following notice thereof.
(Ord. 1977-16, passed 11-7-77)
§ 50.04 DUMPSTERS.
   (A)   Residents of the town shall have the ability to use the dumpsters
provided by the town free of charge.
   (B)   Non-residents of the town shall not be allowed the use of the
dumpsters provided by the town.
   (C)   Individuals using the dumpsters provided by the town shall show proof
of residency through a valid driver’s license and/or recent utility bill.
(Ord. 2007-17, passed 9-24-07)
CHARGES
§ 50.15 UNIT DETERMINATION AND ADJUSTMENT OF SERVICE CHARGE.
   (A)   The billing unit shall be the amount to be charged per year for the
specified service of 52 regular weekly pickups.
   (B)   For the first contract year, the number of units in the town upon
which the compensation to the contractor shall be computed is arbitrarily set
at 950. For the second and subsequent years, the number of dwelling units which
shall be used as the basis upon which the compensation shall be computed shall
be the foregoing figure of 950 to which there shall be added a figure equal to
the number of units constructed or otherwise created within the limits of the
town for the 12 month period immediately preceding November 1 of the year
immediately prior to the contract year for which the computation is made, as
shown by the official residential building permit records in the Albany
Municipal Office.
   (C)   For the computation of dwelling units in apartment buildings for the
year 1977 and thereafter, one apartment unit will be equal to one dwelling
unit. Figures for these computations stall be taken from the building permits
issued for apartments in the town for the 12 months immediately preceding
November 1 of the year immediately prior to the contract year for which the
computation is being made. These building permits shall only apply to buildings
erected within the town limits.
   (D)   Should any territory be annexed to the town, a figure equal to the
actual number of dwelling units therein, on the basis of a physical count
thereof jointly made or caused to be made by the contractor and the town, shall
be added to the above figure as of and effective upon the effective date that
such annexation is complete and final as prescribed in the applicable statute
of the state on annexation, and the compensation shall be forthwith increased
accordingly. Should any territory be annexed after bid closing date and prior
to starting of the contract herein, the dwelling units shall be added to the
first year’s compensation. For the computation of dwelling units in apartment
buildings for the year 1977 and thereafter, and any territory to be annexed to
the town, this shall be done on the basis of one apartment unit being equal to
one dwelling unit.
(Ord. 1977-16, passed 11-7-77)
§ 50.16 RESERVED.
REQUIREMENTS AND REGULATIONS FOR CONTRACTORS
§ 50.30 TERM OF CONTRACT.
   The contract shall be for such term as the Town Council shall from time to
time establish, not to exceed three years per term.
(Ord. 1977-16, passed 11-7-77; Am. Ord. 1986-8, passed 9-22-86)
§ 50.31 ASSIGNMENT OF CONTRACT.
   The contractor shall not assign or sublet the contract as a whole or in part
without the written consent of the town. The consent does not release the
contractor from any obligation or liability under the contract. Violation of
this provision shall result in immediate cancellation of the contract. Any
violation of the contract shall be sufficient cause for the immediate
cancellation of the contract by the Town Council, who may thereupon employ the
necessary labor to perform the work or re-advertise or re-let the work at the
expense of the offending contractor and his or her sureties.
(Ord. 1977-16, passed 11-7-77)
§ 50.32 RESERVED.
§ 50.33 ACCEPTANCE OR REJECTION OF BIDS.
   (A)   The Town Council reserves the right to accept or reject any or all bid
proposals and to waive defects or irregularities in any bid proposal. In
particular, any alteration, erasure or interlineation of the bid proposal or
the contract document shall render the bid proposal or contract document
irregular and subject to rejection by the Board.
   (B)   The Town Council expressly reserves to itself the right to judge the
experience, capability and financial resources of the bidders to successfully
perform a contract as bid and when found unsatisfactory to reject the bid.
(Ord. 1977-16, passed 11-7-77)
§ 50.34 RESERVED.
§ 50.35 PAYMENT FOR SERVICES.
   The town shall pay the contractor once monthly in the amount of one-twelfth
of the annual service charge.
(Ord. 1977-16, passed 11-7-77)
§ 50.36 COLLECTION SERVICE REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   The contractor shall make weekly pickups of garbage and rubbish from
the curb line of residences or property within the town in compliance with
these specifications.
   (B)   Each dwelling unit shall have a maximum of two 96-gallon containers
per weekly pickup, unless additional containers have been arranged with
disposal contractor.
   (C)   Business and/or commercial units shall have four 96-gallon containers
per weekly pickup, unless additional containers have been arranged with
disposal contractor.
(Ord. 1977-16, passed 11-7-77; Am. Ord. 2014-7, passed 5-12-14)
§ 50.37 SERVICE, EQUIPMENT AND FACILITY REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   The contractor shall provide all the necessary and proper equipment to
collect, haul, and dispose of all garbage and rubbish collected according to
these specifications and as defined by this chapter of the town.
   (B)   The contractor shall provide all the employees necessary to collect,
haul, and dispose of all garbage and rubbish collected according to these
specifications.
   (C)   The contractor shall haul to a sanitary landfill of his or her own
choice, the nature and operation of which must comply with the rules and
regulations of the Indiana State Board of Health.
   (D)   The name of the contractor and the truck number of each piece of
equipment operated by the contractor in the performance of the services
described herein shall be conspicuously displayed on each piece of equipment in
letters and numbers of not less than three inches in height and in compliance
with any other applicable ordinance of the town or other law or regulation.
(Ord. 1977-16, passed 11-7-77)
§ 50.38 DISPOSAL OF MATERIALS COLLECTED.
   (A)   All garbage, rubbish, and household rubbish collected by the
contractor shall be moved to a sanitary landfill as per § 50.37(C) and in
approved, enclosed vehicles.
   (B)   If an emergency arises in connection with the disposal operations, the
contractor may, with the authorization of the Town Council, dispose of
collected garbage and refuse in a manner agreed upon between the contractor and
the Town Council.
(Ord. 1977-16, passed 11-7-77)
§ 50.39 BID BOND REQUIREMENT. 
   Each bid shall be accompanied by a bid bond or certified check in the amount
of 5% of the bidder’s proposed total annual service charge. This bond shall be
forfeited if the bidder fails to enter into a contract within 30 days after he
or she is notified his or her bid has been accepted.
(Ord. 1977-16, passed 11-7-77)
§ 50.40 PERFORMANCE BOND REQUIREMENT.
   The contractor shall maintain a performance bond in an amount equal to one
full year contract service charge during the term of the contract, which bond
shall leave surety to the approval of the Town Council.
(Ord. 1977-16, passed 11-7-77)
§ 50.41 INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS.
   (A)   Worker’s compensation. The contractor shall take out and maintain,
during the term of his or her contract, worker’s compensation insurance for all
employees employed to carry out the terms of the contract. This insurance shall
conform to the requirements set forth in Sections 5, 68 and 69 of the Worker’s
Compensation Act, Burns Indiana Annotated Statutes Sections 40-1601 and 40-
1602. This insurance shall conform to all state law requirements, including,
but not limited to I.C. 22-3-5.
   (B)   Public liability and property damage. The contractor shall take out
and maintain during the term of the contract such public liability and property
damage insurance to protect him or her and any subcontractor performing work
under the contract from claims for damages for personal injury, including
accidental death, as well as from claims for property damage which may arise
from operations under the contract, whether such operations be by himself or
herself or any subcontractor or by anyone directly or indirectly employed by
either of them. The amounts of the insurance shall be as follows:
      (1)   Public liability insurance in an amount not less than $100,000 for
injuries, including accidental death to any one person, and subject to the same
limit for each person in an amount not less than $300,000 on account of one
accident; and
      (2)   Property damage in an amount of not less than $50,000.
   (C)   Certificate of insurance requirement. The contractor shall furnish the
town a certificate of compliance with all the foregoing insurance requirements.
Failure to do so is cause for immediate cancellation of the contract.
(Ord. 1977-16, passed 11-7-77)
§ 50.42 INDEMNITY REQUIREMENT.
   The contractor shall hold harmless from and indemnify the town against all
claims, suits, actions, costs, counsel fees, expenses, damages, judgments or
decrees by reason of any person or persons or property being damaged or injured
by the contractor or any of his or her subcontractors, or any person employed
under the contractor, or under any of his or her subcontractors, or in any
capacity during the progress of the services defined herein.
(Ord. 1977-16, passed 11-7-77)
§ 50.43 COLLECTION OF LARGE REFUSE ITEMS.
   (A)   The town shall provide collection services for large refuse items that
are not "garbage", "household rubbish" or "rubbish" items as defined in Ord.
1977-16.
   (B)   Individuals shall contact the town municipal office to request that
the town collect the large refuse items from their residence or business prior
to setting the large refuse item out for collection.
   (C)   Individuals shall be charged a fee for having the town collect the
large refuse item. This charge is in addition to the fee that is paid for the
collection of garbage, household rubbish and rubbish.
   (D)   The town shall determine the amount of fee to be charged for the
collection of the large refuse items. Said fees may be changed from time to
time by the Town Council. The current fee schedule shall be kept at the town
municipal office and is attached to Ord. 2014-7 and made a part of said
ordinance. Individuals shall pay the collection charge prior to having the
large refuse item being collected.
   (E)   In the event that individuals put large refuse items out for
collection prior to contacting the town municipal office requesting collection
of the same and before paying the collection charges as to the same, the town
shall place a notice on the door to the individual's residence and place a
notice on the individual's mailbox giving the individual a week to go to the
town municipal office to pay the collection charges.
   (F)   In the event that the individual fails to respond to the notice posted
on their door within a week, the town shall pick up the large refuse item the
next collection day and shall add the collection charge to the individual's
next utility bill.
(Ord. 2014-7, passed 5-12-14)
