CHAPTER 94: PARKS
Section
   
94.01   Closing times
   
94.02   Hours posted
   
94.03   Violation
   
94.04   Rules and regulations
   
94.05   Park usage
 
   
94.99   Penalty
   
Appendix A: Park grounds rental agreement
§ 94.01 CLOSING TIMES.
   The town parks shall be closed to the public between the hours of 11:00 p.m.
and 6:00 a.m., local time, each and every day.
(Ord. 1971-22, passed 9-27-71)
§ 94.02 HOURS POSTED.
   The hours during which the parks are to be closed shall be posted at the
entrance to each town park.
(Ord. 1971-22, passed 9-27-71)
§ 94.03 VIOLATION.
   Any person violating this chapter by entering, using, or occupying any town
park during the hours same is closed shall be punished as set forth in §
94.99.
(Ord. 1971-22, passed 9-27-71) Penalty, see §
94.99
§ 94.04 RULES AND REGULATIONS.
   (A)   The purpose of this section is to establish reasonable and responsible
rules for those individuals who use the parks and other recreational areas
owned and operated by the town. This section is necessary to insure that
residents fully enjoy leisure and recreational activities available in Albany
parks and other recreational areas and to protect health and safety of persons
using the parks and other recreational areas.
   (B)   The words “parks and other recreation areas” shall include, but not be
limited to, any lands, buildings, structures, waters, parks, trails, drives and
roadways in the town that are under the jurisdiction and control of the town
and the Albany Parks Department.
   (C)   Individuals listed on State of Indiana Sex Offenders Registry
published and disseminated by the Indiana Criminal Justice Institute are
prohibited from all parks and other recreational areas of the town.
(Ord. 2008-15, passed 11-10-08)
§ 94.05 PARK USAGE.
   (A)   The town shall allow the following park areas to be used by
individuals and organizations for events: Big Park, Depot, Water Street Park
and First Street Park.
   (B)   The town shall require individuals and organizations who want to use
the park areas for events to enter into an agreement with the town for the use
of the park area.
   (C)   The town may require the individuals and groups to provide a damage
deposit for the usage of the park area. The requirement of the damage deposit
and the amount of the damage deposit shall be determined by the Clerk-Treasurer
in a case-by-case manner.
   (D)   The town shall require the individuals and groups using the park area
to provide proof of insurance reflecting that the individuals or group holding
the event is covered by insurance.
   (E)   The town shall require the individuals and groups using the park for
events to sign a statement that they will hold the town harmless from any
injuries and damages that may occur as a result of what takes place at the
event.
   (F)   The town may deny the use of the park areas to individuals and groups
for events in the event that the individuals and groups refuse to comply with
the town’s requirements under this section.
(Ord. 2009-7, passed 6-8-09)
§ 94.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Whoever violates this chapter is guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction thereof, shall be fined in an amount not exceeding $10 per
violation.
   (B)   Any person who violates §
94.04(C) shall be fined $100 for the first offense and $200 for each offense
thereafter. A separate offense shall be deemed committed for each day during
which or on which a violation occurs or continues to occur.
(Ord. 1971-22, passed 9-27-71; Am. Ord. 2008-15, passed 11-10-08)

between the Town of Albany, Indiana, hereinafter referred to as “Owner,” and
                        of                            , Indiana, hereinafter
referred to as “Renter”, for the town’s park grounds, hereinafter referred to
as “Premises”, under the following terms and conditions:
   1.   The renter agrees to pay owner the sum of $                          
for rental of Big/Depot/Water Street/1st Street park grounds. (Please circle
which specific park ground this agreement applies to.) Said amount shall be
paid as follows: A damage deposit in the sum of $                  is due and
owing upon the signing of this Rental Agreement. The remainder of the amount
due and owing to the owner shall be paid on the                        day of
                            , 200    . Payment for all obligations shall be

                                  day of                              , 20

and of any other person(s) involved in the activities or event.

that the renter assigns space to or sublets space for display, and the like.
   8.   Renter shall provide appropriate security and police services, as
required or necessary to properly control the activity or event.
   9.   The parties agree that this agreement does not constitute an agency
relationship between the parties.
   10.   The renter shall save, defend, hold harmless and indemnify the owner
from all claims (both threatened and asserted) for damages to persons or to
property arising from the renter’s occupancy of the premises, including, but
not limited to, all judgments, settlements or awards which might be entered for
such claims, and also including, but not limited to, all attorneys fees the
owner incurs as the result of the threat or the assertion of any claim.
   11.   This Rental Agreement, and the rights and obligations of the parties
hereto, shall be interpreted and construed in accordance with the laws of
Indiana.

CHAPTER 95: GOLF CARTS
Section
   
95.01   Operation of golf carts
   
95.02   Registration of golf carts
   
95.03   Revocation or suspension of golf cart registration
 
   
95.99   Penalty
§ 95.01 OPERATION OF GOLF CARTS.
   (A)   A GOLF CART is a gas or electric motorized four wheeled cart designed
to carry people and/or materials.
   (B)   The operation of golf carts are permitted within the boundaries of the
town, only upon compliance with the requirements set forth in this chapter.
   (C)   No person shall operate a golf cart within the boundaries of the town
without first completing each of the following provisions:
      (1)   The operator must be 18 years of age or older;
      (2)   The operator must have a valid identification card, operator's
license, chauffeur's license or public passenger chauffeur's license issued by
the Indiana Bureau of Motor Vehicles;
      (3)   The operator shall allow the Town Marshal or a representative of
the office of the Town Marshal to inspect the golf cart; and
      (4)   The operator shall provide the Town Marshal or a representative of
the office of the Town Marshal with proof of financial responsibility.
   (D)   The Town Marshal or a representative of the office of the Town Marshal
shall issue a three-digit identification number to the operator of the golf
cart after all of the requirements of division (C) have been met. The
identification number shall be placed on all four sides of the golf cart in a
visible location, using three-inch numbers.
   (E)   The operator of the golf cart shall place a slow moving vehicle sign
on the rear of the golf cart.
   (F)   Golf carts shall be equipped with two headlights and two taillights.
These headlights and taillights shall be operated at all times during operation
of the golf cart.
   (G)   Golf carts shall be equipped with a rear-view mirror.
   (H)   Golf carts shall only be operated on the streets and roadways of the
town. Travel on Highways 28 and 67 shall be strictly restricted. The golf carts
shall only travel across Highways 28 and 67. The golf carts shall only travel
adjacent to Highways 28 and 67 for short distances in order to gain access to
town streets and highways.
   (I)   Golf carts shall not be operated on any sidewalk located within the
boundaries of the town.
   (J)   The operator of the golf cart shall abide by and follow all Indiana
motor vehicles laws.
   (K)   The operator of the golf cart shall yield to all motor vehicle
traffic.
(Ord. 2002-18, passed 11-25-02)
§ 95.02 REGISTRATION OF GOLF CARTS.
   (A)   Operation. All golf carts shall be operated under the following
requirements:
      (1)   The operator must be at least 18 years of age and have a valid
identification card, operator’s license, chauffeur’s license or public
passenger chauffeur’s license issued by the Indiana Bureau of Motor Vehicles.
      (2)   The operator shall allow the Town Marshal or a representative of
the office of the Town Marshal to inspect a golf cart to ensure that it
functions properly and has the required safety equipment.
      (3)   The operator of the golf cart shall provide the Town Marshal or
their representative with proof of insurance that covers the operation of the
golf cart.
      (4)   Pay a registration fee, annually each January, of $20 for each golf
cart operated.
   (B)   Registration fee; proof of registration.
      (1)   Upon satisfactory completion of the inspection of the golf cart by
the Town Marshal or their representative, the Town Marshal shall issue a three-
digit identification number to the operator.
      (2)   The registration number shall be affixed to the golf cart by the
operator on the rear of the golf cart and in a location that is readily visible
to law enforcement.
      (3)   The operator of the golf cart shall be responsible for obtaining
and renewing the registration on all golf carts that operate in the town.
(Ord. 2024-12, passed 12-9-2024)
§ 95.03 REVOCATION OR SUSPENSION OF GOLF CART REGISTRATION.
   (A)   The Town Marshal or their representative may revoke or suspend the
registration of the operator’s golf cart operation privileges in the town for
the following reasons:
      (1)   Unsafe operation of the golf cart;
      (2)   Issuance of more than three citations issued by the Police
Department for violation of the town ordinances of the operation of the golf
cart;
      (3)   The condition of the golf cart is such that it is unsafe to operate
on the streets and alleys in the town;
      (4)   If any of the safety features are inoperable;
      (5)   The suspension, revocation of the operator’s driving privileges by
the State of Indiana;
      (6)   The failure to maintain proper insurance on the golf cart;
      (7)   Any suspension of the operator’s privileges to operate a golf cart
in the town may be for a period of time to correct any issue with the vehicle
or address any other concern of the Town Marshal.
   (B)   Appeal of revocation.
      (1)   Any person who has had their privileges suspended or revoked by the
Town Marshal may appeal the suspension or revocation to the Town Council within
ten days, in writing and delivered to the Clerk-Treasurer either in person or
via regular first-class mail.
      (2)   The Town Council shall schedule a meeting/hearing on the appeal at
the next Town Council meeting. If the person appealing the suspension or
revocation shall fail to appear at the Town Council meeting, then the appeal
shall automatically be denied.
      (3)   A decision of the Town Council to uphold the suspension or
revocation of the person’s golf cart operating privileges may be appealed to
the Circuit Court of Delaware County within 15 days of the decision of the Town
Council.
(Ord. 2024-12, passed 12-9-2024)
§ 95.99 PENALTY.
   A violation of this chapter may result in the following penalties:
   (A)   A fine in the sum of $50 for the first offense;
   (B)   A fine in the sum of $75 for the second offense;
   (C)   A fine in the sum of $100 for the third or subsequent offenses.
(Ord. 2002-18, passed 11-25-02)
CHAPTER 96: FIREWORKS
Section
   
96.01   Definitions
   
96.02   Regulation as to time and dates of use of consumer fireworks
   
96.03   Required cleanup of consumer fireworks
§ 96.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For purposes of this chapter the following definitions shall apply unless
the context clearly indicates of requires a different meaning.
   CONSUMER FIREWORKS.  
      (1)   A small firework that is designed primarily to produce visible
effects by combustion, and that is required to comply with the construction,
chemical composition and labeling regulations promulgated by the United States
Consumer Product Safety Commission. The term also includes some small devices
designed to produce an audible effect, such as whistling devices, ground
devices containing 50 milligrams or less of explosive composition and aerial
devices containing 130 milligrams or less of explosive composition.
      (2)   CONSUMER FIREWORKS include:
         (a)   Aerial devices, which include sky rockets, missile type rockets,
helicopter or aerial spinners, roman candles, mines and shells; and
         (b)   Ground audible devices, which include firecrackers, salutes and
chasers.
(Ord. 2007-13, passed 7-23-07)
§ 96.02 REGULATION AS TO TIME AND DATES OF USE OF CONSUMER FIREWORKS.
   No person shall use and/or ignite any consumer fireworks inside the
corporate boundaries of the town during times other than:
   (A)   Between the hours of 5:00 p.m. and two hours after sunset on June 29,
June 30, July 1, July 2, July 3, July 5, July 6, July 7, July 8 and July 9;
   (B)   Between the hours of 10:00 a.m. and 12:00 midnight on July 4; and
   (C)   Between the hours of 10:00 a.m. on December 31 and 1:00 a.m. on
January 1.
(Ord. 2007-13, passed 7-23-07)
§ 96.03 REQUIRED CLEANUP OF CONSUMER FIREWORKS.
   No person shall cause the used consumer fireworks products to remain on town
property or in the town rights-of-way. Any person who leaves used consumer
fireworks products on town property or in the town rights-of-way shall be fined
the sum of $50.
(Ord. 2007-13, passed 7-23-07)

GENERAL PROVISIONS
§ 110.01 HANDGUN LICENSES.
   (A)   The Police Department of the town is authorized pursuant to law, I.C.
35-47-2-3(b) et seq., to take applications for handgun licenses and to collect
an application fee as follows:
License Type Local Fee
License Type                                        Local Fee
Five year hunting and target                        $0/$0 refundable*
Five year personal protection                       $0/$0 refundable*
Lifetime hunting and target/ no current license     $50/$30 refundable*
Lifetime hunting and target/ current valid license  $40/$30 refundable*
Lifetime personal protection/ no current license    $50/$30 refundable*
Lifetime personal protection/ current valid license $40/$30 refundable*

   (B)   The application fees collected shall be deposited by the Clerk-

   (C)   The application procedure and disbursement of funds shall be in

(Ord. 1985-1, passed 2-25-85; Am. Ord. 2006-14, passed 8-29-06; Am. Ord. 2020-

RUMMAGE SALES
§ 110.15 DEFINITION.
   (A)   A RUMMAGE SALE is the sale of personal property by an individual or
family at their own personal residence or the residence of others for the
purpose of the sale of surplus personal property, clothing, or other items
belonging to the person commonly known as the homeowner. The sale is only
conducted in an area that is zoned as “residential.”
   (B)   RUMMAGE SALE does not include the sale of one motor vehicle by an
individual or family at their own personal residence or the residence of others
for the purpose of the sale of the motor vehicle.
(Ord. 1998-5, passed 4-27-98; Am. Ord. 2004-2, passed 1-26-04)
§ 110.16 LIMITATIONS ON DAYS OF SALES.
   A person may only conduct a rummage sale for no more than four consecutive
days for any one sale. A person may conduct no more than three rummage sales
per year with a 90-day waiting period commencing after the completion of the
prior rummage sale.
(Ord. 1998-5, passed 4-27-98; Am. Ord. 2019- 16, passed 11-11-19) Penalty, see
§
110.99
§ 110.17 CONCLUSION OF SALE.
   Any rummage sale shall be concluded at the end of the fourth day, and all
property not sold shall be either discarded or stored inside a structure or
building. The owner may not cover the property with a cloth, plastic, or other
type of covering and await the end of the 90-day period for the next rummage
sale to commence.
(Ord. 1998-5, passed 4-27-98; Am. Ord. 2019- 16, passed 11-11-19) Penalty, see
§
110.99
§ 110.18 ENFORCEMENT.
   The town may enforce this subchapter by use of an injunction or any other
legal remedy, including a fine.
(Ord. 1998-5, passed 4-27-98)
§ 110.99 PENALTY.
   (A)   Whoever violates a provision of this chapter for which no specific
penalty is provided shall be punished as set forth in §
10.99.
   (B)   A violation of §§
110.15 et seq. may result in a fine from $0 up to $500. Each day that the
property owner is in violation of §§
110.15 et seq. shall constitute a separate offense.
(Ord. 1998-5, passed 4-27-98)
CHAPTER 111: TRANSIENT MERCHANTS
Section
   
111.01   Definitions
   
111.02   License requirement
   
111.03   Application procedure
   
111.04   Standards for issuance
   
111.05   Revocation procedure
   
111.06   Standards for revocation
   
111.07   Appeal procedure
   
111.08   Exhibition of identification
Statutory reference:
   Local regulation authorized, see I.C. 25-37-1-11
§ 111.01 DEFINITIONS.
   For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply
unless the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
   BUSINESS. The business carried on by any person who is a transient merchant
as defined in this section.
   GOODS. Merchandise of any description whatsoever and includes, but is not
limited to, wares and foodstuffs.
   TRANSIENT MERCHANT.  
      (1)   All persons, firms, limited liability companies, and corporations,
both as principals and agents, who engage in, do, or transact any temporary or
transient business in the corporate boundaries of the town offering for sale or
selling goods, wares, or merchandise and those who, for the purpose of carrying
on such business, hire, lease, or occupy any permanent or mobile building,
structure, or real estate for the exhibition by means of samples, catalogs,
photographs, and price lists for sale of such goods, wares, or merchandise.
      (2)   TRANSIENT MERCHANT does not include the following:
         (a)   Any person, individual, co-partner, limited liability company or
corporation which grows the goods, wares, or merchandise that are sold or
offered for sale;
         (b)   A person who makes crafts or items by hand and sells them or
offers them for sale;
         (c)   An auctioneer who is licensed under the law of the State of
Indiana;
         (d)   A resident of the Town of Albany who conducts a sale of tangible
personal property for no more than four work days per calendar year;
         (e)   An organization that is exempt from the Indiana gross retail
tax;
         (f)   A person who:
            1.   Sells merchandise;
            2.   Offers to sell merchandise; and
            3.   Provides proof that the sale is being conducted as part of an
activity sponsored by an organization that is exempt from the Indiana gross
retail tax;
         (g)   A person who;
            1.   Organizes;
            2.   Sells merchandise at;
            3.   Offers to sell merchandise at; or
            4.   Exhibits at a trade show or conventions.
         (h)   A person who holds a registered retail merchants certificate.
         (i)   Residents of the Town of Albany who wish to conduct temporary or
transient business within the corporate boundaries.
(Am. Ord. 2004-6, passed 2-23-04)
§ 111.02 LICENSE REQUIREMENT.
   (A)   Any person who is a transient merchant shall obtain a license before
engaging in such activity within the corporate boundaries of the Town of
Albany.
   (B)   The fee for the license required by this chapter shall be $25.
   (C)   No license issued under this chapter shall be transferable.
   (D)   All licenses issued under this chapter shall expire six months after
the date of issuance thereof. The provisions of this chapter shall not apply to
sales made to dealers or commercial travelers or selling agents in the usual
course of business nor to bona fide sales of goods, wares or merchandise by
sample for future delivery, or sheriffs, constables or other public officers
selling goods, wares and merchandise according to law, nor to bona fide
assignees or receivers appointed in the State of Indiana selling goods, wares
and merchandise for the benefit of creditors.
(Am. Ord. 2004-6, passed 2-23-04) Penalty, see §
10.99
§ 111.03 APPLICATION PROCEDURE.
   (A)   All applicants for licenses required by this chapter shall file an
application with the Clerk. This application shall be signed by the applicant
if an individual, or by all partners if a partnership, or by the president if a
corporation. The applicant may be requested to provide information concerning
the following items:
      (1)   The name, residence and post office address of the person, firm,
limited liability company or corporation making the application;
      (2)   (a)   The name of the individual having management authority or
supervision of the applicant’s business during the time that it is proposed to
be carried on in the town;
         (b)   The local address of such individual;
         (c)   The permanent address of such individual; and
         (d)   The capacity in which such individual will act.
      (3)   If the applicant is a corporation or limited liability company, the
state of incorporation or organization, the date of incorporation or
organization, and if the applicant is a corporation or a limited liability
company formed in a state other than the State of Indiana, the date on which
such corporation or limited liability company qualified to transact business as
a foreign corporation or foreign limited liability company in the State of
Indiana.
      (4)   The time period or periods in which it is proposed to carry on
applicant's business.
      (5)   A statement showing the kind of business purposed to be conducted
and if for the purpose of transacting such business any permanent mobile
building, structure or real estate is to be used for the exhibition by means of
samples, catalogs, photographs and price lists or sales of goods, wares or
merchandise, the location of such proposed place of business.
      (6)   A detailed inventory and description of such goods, wares, and
merchandise to be offered for sale or sold, the manner in which the same is to
be advertised for sale and the representations to be made in connections
therewith, the names of the persons from whom the goods, wares, merchandise so
to be advertised or represented were obtained, the date of such receipt of such
goods, wares and merchandise by the applicant for the license, the place from
which the same were last taken and any and all details necessary to locate and
identify all goods, wares and merchandise to be sold.
      (7)   A statement as to whether or not the applicant has been convicted
of any crime or misdemeanor and, if so, the nature of each offense and the
penalty assessed for each offense.
   (B)   The applicant shall attach to the application a receipt showing that
personal property taxes on the goods, wares, merchandise to be offered for sale
or sold have been paid.
   (C)   The applicant shall attach to the application a criminal history
report completed by the Delaware County Sheriff’s Department or any other
Sheriff’s Department for the applicant if the applicant is an individual, each
partner if the applicant is a partnership and each officer if the applicant is
a corporation or limited liability company.
(Am. Ord. 2004-6, passed 2-23-04; Am. Ord. 2010-7, passed 8-23-10) Penalty, see
§
10.99
§ 111.04 STANDARDS FOR ISSUANCE.
   (A)   Upon receipt of an application, the Town Marshal or his or her
representatives shall review the applicant’s criminal history report.
   (B)   The application shall be approved unless the review of the applicant’s
criminal history discloses tangible evidence that the conduct of the
applicant’s business would pose a substantial threat to the public health,
safety, morals, or general welfare. In particular, tangible evidence that the
applicant has done any of the following will constitute valid reasons for
disapproval of an application:
      (1)   Has been convicted of a crime of moral turpitude;
      (2)   Has made willful misstatements in the application;
      (3)   Has committed prior violations of ordinances pertaining to
itinerant or transient merchants, peddlers, solicitors, and the like;
      (4)   Has committed prior fraudulent acts; or
      (5)   Has a record of continual breaches of solicited contracts.
   (C)   There shall be a seven-day waiting period from the date the completed
application is submitted to the Clerk and the date on which the decision to
approve or disapprove the application is made.
(Am. Ord. 2004-6, passed 2-23-04; Am. Ord. 2010-7, passed 8-23-10)
§ 111.05 REVOCATION PROCEDURE.
   Any license or permit granted under this chapter may be revoked by the Clerk
after notice and hearing, pursuant to the standards in §
111.06. Notice of hearing for revocation shall be given in writing, setting
forth specifically the grounds of the complaint and the time and place of the
hearing. The notice shall be mailed to the licensee at his or her last known
address, at least ten days prior to the date set for the hearing.
§ 111.06 STANDARDS FOR REVOCATION.
   A license granted under this chapter may be revoked for any of the following
reasons:
   (A)   Any fraud or misrepresentation contained in the license application;
   (B)   Any fraud, misrepresentation, or false statement made in connection
with the business being conducted under the license;
   (C)   Any violation of this chapter;
   (D)   Conviction of the licensee of any felony or conviction of the licensee
of any misdemeanor involving moral turpitude; or
   (E)   Conducting the business licensed in an unlawful manner or in such a
way as to constitute a menace to the health, safety, morals, or general welfare
of the public.
§ 111.07 APPEAL PROCEDURE.
   (A)   Any person aggrieved by a decision under §§
111.04 or
111.06 shall have the right to appeal to the Town Council. The appeal shall be
taken by filing with the Town Council, within 14 days after notice of the
decision has been mailed to such person’s last known address, a written
statement setting forth the grounds for appeal. The Town Council shall set the
time and place for a hearing, and notice for the hearing shall be given to the
person in the same manner as provided in §
111.05.
   (B)   The order of the Town Council after the hearing shall be final.
§ 111.08 EXHIBITION OF IDENTIFICATION.
   Any license issued to a transient merchant under this chapter shall be kept
on file at the Albany Town Hall.
(Am. Ord. 2004-6, passed 2-23-04)
CHAPTER 112: CABLE REGULATIONS
Section
   
112.01   FCC rules and regulations adopted
   
112.02   Public hearing
   
112.03   Rate review period
   
112.04   Review of basic service tier and necessary equipment
   
112.05   Town Council’s decision
   
112.06   Confidentiality of information
   
112.07   Refunds
 
   
112.99   Penalty
§ 112.01 FCC RULES AND REGULATIONS ADOPTED.
   (A)   The Town Council and Council members adopt the rules and regulations
set forth by the Federal Communications Commission pursuant to Section 623(b)
of the Cable Television Consumer Protection and Competition Act of 1992 (47 USC
543 (b)) for the review of the basic service tier of cable television services
and equipment necessary for the provision of the service tier.
   (B)   For the purposes of this chapter, the basic service tier of cable
television services shall mean a separately available service tier to which
subscription is required for access to any other tier of service, including as
a minimum, but not limited to, all signals of domestic television broadcast
stations provided to any subscriber, (except a signal secondarily transmitted
by satellite carrier beyond the local service area of the station, regardless
of how the signal is ultimately received by the cable system) any public,
educational, and governmental programming required by the franchise to be
carried on the basic tier, and any additional video programming signals or
service added to the basic tier by the cable operator. Equipment necessary to
provide the basic tier of service shall be defined as those items of associated
equipment necessary for the reception of basic cable service by a subscriber,
including, but not limited to converter boxes, remote control units, additional
outlets and installations.
(Ord. 1993-19, passed 11-8-93) Penalty, see §
112.99
§ 112.02 PUBLIC HEARING.
   (A)   The town shall provide the grantee of the cable television franchise,
the public, and interested parties with an opportunity to be heard at a public
hearing before the Town Council, upon 14 days written notice to the grantee of
the cable television franchise of the time and place of the public hearing;
provided further, that the notice shall indicate that the purpose of the public
hearing is to receive the views of the grantee and interested parties on issues
pertaining to regulation of the basic service tier of cable television services
and equipment necessary to provide the basic tier of service; and provided
further, that notice of the public hearing shall be published in a local
newspaper of general circulation at least ten days before the date of this
hearing; and provided further, that an agenda for the public hearing shall be
posted in a public place at the Albany Municipal Office at least seven days
prior to the public hearing.
   (B)   Upon the adoption of this chapter and the certification of the town by
the Federal Communications Commission, the town shall immediately notify the
cable operator by certified mail, return receipt requested, that the town
intends to regulate subscriber rates charged for the basic service tier and
associated equipment as authorized by the Cable Television Consumer Protection
and Competition Act of 1992. Upon receipt of the notice by the town, the cable
operator shall, within 30 days, file with the town its current rates for the
basic service tier and associated equipment along with any additional
documentation justifying the reasonableness of its rates.
(Ord. 1993-19, passed 11-8-93)
§ 112.03 RATE REVIEW PERIOD.
   (A)   The town shall establish that the period for review of rates of the
basic service tier of cable television services and the equipment necessary to
provide the basic tier of service shall be 30 days from the submission by the
grantee of the cable television franchise of Federal Communications Commission
Form 393. If the Town Council takes no action within 30 days from the date the
cable operator files its basic cable rates with the town, the proposed rates
will continue in effect.
   (B)   In the event that additional time for review of the Federal
Communications Commission Form 393 submitted by grantee is necessary, the Town
Council or their designee shall issue a brief written order prior to the end of
the 30-day review period, with a copy of the order to be sent by certified
United States Mail to the grantee, providing for an additional 90-day period
for review of rates of the basic service tier and the equipment necessary to
provide the basic tier of service. During the extended review period and before
taking action on the proposed rate, the Town Council shall hold at least one
public hearing in which interested citizens may express their views and record
objections.
(Ord. 1993-19, passed 11-8-93)
§ 112.04 REVIEW OF BASIC SERVICE TIER AND NECESSARY EQUIPMENT.
   (A)   The town shall establish that, after a cable operator has submitted
for review its existing rates for the basic service tier and associated
equipment costs, or a proposed increase in these rates (including increases in
the baseline channel change that results from reductions in the number of
channels in a tier), the existing rates will remain in effect or the proposed
rates will become effective after 30 days from the date of submission; provided
however, that the town may toll this 30-day deadline for an additional time by
issuing a brief written order as described in division (B) of this section
within 30 days of the rate submission explaining that it needs additional time
to review the rates.
   (B)   If the town is unable to determine, based upon the material submitted
by the cable operator, that the existing or proposed rates are within the
Commission’s permitted basic service tier charge or actual cost of equipment,
or if a cable operator has submitted a cost-of-service showing seeking to
justify a rate above the Commission’s basic service tier charge, the town may
toll the 30-day deadline in division (A) of this section to request and/or
consider the comments from interested parties as follows:
      (1)   For an additional 90 days in cases not involving cost-of-service
showings; or
      (2)   For an additional 150 days in cases involving cost-of-service
showings.
(Ord. 1993-19, passed 11-8-93; Am. Ord. 1995-9, passed 6-12-95)
§ 112.05 TOWN COUNCIL’S DECISION.
   (A)   Upon completion of its review of the proposed rates for the basic
service tier of cable television services and the equipment necessary to
provide the basic tier of service, the Town Council shall adopt its decision by
formal resolution. The resolution shall indicate the reasons for the decision.
Upon passage of the resolution, the Town Council shall publish the resolution
in pamphlet form.
   (B)   In the event that the cable operator’s proposed rates exceed the
reasonable rate standard as established by the Federal Communications
Commission in its rules and regulations attached hereto, the Town Council may
order the rates reduced by roll backs or refunds to subscribers in the manner
so prescribed by the Federal Communications Commission.
(Ord. 1993-19, passed 11-8-93)
§ 112.06 CONFIDENTIALITY OF INFORMATION.
   In considering information provided by the grantee as a part of review of
his or her rates for the basic service tier of cable television services and
the equipment necessary to provide the basic tier of service, the town shall
not disclose to the public the content of any records, forms, reports,
calculations, or other documents as provided which the grantee has indicated as
being of a proprietary interest or constituting a trade secret in nature. The
municipal officer responsible for administration of the Indiana Freedom of
Information Act shall retain the right to determine the validity of the
grantee’s claim of proprietary interest or trade secrecy in accordance with the
provisions of the Indiana Freedom of Information Act.
(Ord. 1993-19, passed 11-8-93)
§ 112.07 REFUNDS.
   The town may order the cable operator to refund to subscribers a portion of
previously paid rates under the following circumstances:
   (A)   A portion of the previously paid rates have been determined to lie in
excess of the permitted basic cable service tier charge or above the actual
cost of equipment; or
   (B)   The cable operator has failed to comply with a valid rate order issued
by the town.
(Ord. 1993-19, passed 11-8-93)
§ 112.99 PENALTY.
   Failure by the cable operator to comply with the terms and conditions
established by this chapter shall constitute a violation of this chapter. The
penalty for the violations of this section are subject to the provisions of §
10.99.
(Ord. 1993-19, passed 11-8-93)
